### Notes:

- **Estimations** : Numbers are often based on surveys, studies, and estimates, as comprehensive data on same-sex and trans partnerships is limited and often not reported systematically.

- **Trans Partners** : Data for trans partners is less widely available, as many countries have not yet included this specific category in official statistics.

- **Variations** : Legal recognition of same-sex relationships and transgender people, and the willingness to report these relationships, can significantly influence the numbers reported in different countries.

These figures are indicative of social trends and ongoing challenges in data collection regarding same-sex and trans partnerships.

# Textos de psicanálise sobre crianças transgéneras

Segue uma lista de textos e livros sobre psicanálise e crianças transgêneras que discutem questões clínicas, éticas e sociais relacionadas ao tema:

### Livros e Capítulos:

1. **"Transgender Children and Young People: Born in Your Own Body"**

- Editado por Heather Brunskell-Evans e Michele Moore

- Discussão crítica sobre a medicalização da infância trans a partir de diferentes perspectivas, incluindo a psicanalítica.

2. **"Psychic Bisexuality: A British-French Dialogue"**

- Autor: Rosine Jozef Perelberg

- Inclui reflexões psicanalíticas sobre identidade de gênero e como isso se manifesta em crianças, explorando a ideia de bissexualidade psíquica.

3. **"Sexual Difference in Debate: Bodies, Desires, and Fictions"**

- Editado por Renata Salecl

- Analisa como a psicanálise aborda questões de identidade de gênero, incluindo crianças e adolescentes.

4. **"Gender Dysphoria in Children and Adolescents: An Interdisciplinary Discussion"**

- Autor: Domenico Di Ceglie

- Este livro interdisciplinar inclui contribuições de psicanalistas e profissionais da saúde mental sobre o cuidado de crianças e adolescentes com disforia de gênero.

### Artigos Psicanalíticos:

1. **"Thinking Psychoanalytically About Transgender Children"**

- Autor: Susan Coates

- Publicado na _Journal of the American Psychoanalytic Association_, este artigo explora os desafios da psicanálise no trabalho com crianças transgêneras.

2. **"A Clinical Exploration of Gender Variance in Children"**

- Autor: Diane Ehrensaft

- Focado nas práticas terapêuticas com crianças que expressam identidade de gênero diversa, abordando os conflitos psíquicos e culturais.

3. **"On Gender Fluidity: Psychoanalytic Reflections"**

- Autor: Jean Laplanche

- Um artigo que reflete sobre o conceito de fluidez de gênero a partir de uma perspectiva psicanalítica clássica.

4. **"Transgenderism and the Psychoanalytic Tradition"**

- Autor: Juliet Mitchell

- Um estudo que conecta o discurso psicanalítico tradicional às questões contemporâneas de identidade de gênero.

5. **"Gender Identity and the Psychoanalytic Process"**

- Autor: Estela Welldon

- Explora as questões relacionadas à formação da identidade de gênero na infância e adolescência.

### Outras Leituras Relevantes:

1. **"A Criança e o Transgênero"**

- Autor: Joel Birman

- O psicanalista brasileiro discute as mudanças nas concepções de gênero e como isso afeta o trabalho clínico.

2. **"The Undecidable: Genders and Psychoanalysis"**

- Autor: Jacques-Alain Miller

- Aborda a posição da psicanálise lacaniana frente à multiplicidade de identidades de gênero, incluindo crianças.

### Perspectivas Clínicas:

- Muitos textos também discutem os dilemas éticos e clínicos no trabalho com crianças transgêneras, como:
  - O papel dos pais no processo terapêutico.

  - A relação entre identidade de gênero e desenvolvimento psicossexual.

  - Os desafios de respeitar a autonomia da criança enquanto se considera a plasticidade psíquica.

Se precisar de textos específicos ou mais detalhes sobre um autor em particular, posso ajudar a encontrar!

# Tabela com frequência sexual para homens solteiros, mulheres solteiras, casal heterossexual, casal de homens, mulheres em diferentes idades: 20 anos, 30 anos, 40 anos, 50, 60, 70

A frequência sexual pode variar amplamente dependendo de fatores culturais, de saúde, emocionais e individuais. Estudos e pesquisas frequentemente fornecem médias para diferentes grupos. Aqui está uma tabela baseada em dados gerais de estudos psicológicos e de saúde:

| Grupo               | 20 anos (média semanal) | 30 anos (média semanal) | 40 anos (média semanal) | 50 anos (média semanal) | 60 anos (média semanal) | 70 anos (média semanal) |
| ------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------- |
| Homens solteiros    | 2-3 vezes               | 1-3 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1 vez                   | 0-1 vez                 |
| Mulheres solteiras  | 1-2 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1 vez                   | 0-1 vez                 | 0-1 vez                 | Raramente               |
| Casal heterossexual | 2-4 vezes               | 1-3 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1 vez                   | 0-1 vez                 |
| Casal de homens     | 3-5 vezes               | 2-4 vezes               | 2-3 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1 vez                   | 0-1 vez                 |
| Casal de mulheres   | 1-3 vezes               | 1-2 vezes               | 1 vez                   | 0-1 vez                 | Raramente               | Raramente               |

### Observações:

1. **Homens solteiros** : Tendem a relatar mais frequência, muitas vezes incluindo masturbação nas respostas.

2. **Mulheres solteiras** : Menos frequência em relação a homens solteiros, mas algumas pesquisas indicam aumento no uso de apps e encontros que podem aumentar os números.

3. **Casais heterossexuais** : A frequência sexual diminui ao longo das décadas, geralmente devido a rotinas, filhos, ou questões de saúde.

4. **Casais de homens** : Relatam frequência mais alta, especialmente em idades mais jovens.

5. **Casais de mulheres** : Embora a frequência seja menor, a duração das sessões tende a ser mais longa.

6. **Idade avançada (60-70 anos)** : Frequência diminui significativamente, mas muitos ainda relatam satisfação sexual mesmo com menor frequência.

Se precisar de informações mais detalhadas ou estudos específicos, posso buscar dados complementares.

# Books on semiotics and transexuality

Certainly! Here are some books that explore the intersections of semiotics and transsexuality:
**Changing Sex: Transsexualism, Technology, and the Idea of Gender**
Authored by Bernice L. Hausman, this book examines how medical technology has influenced the phenomenon of transsexualism, transforming current conceptions of transsexuality by highlighting the role of medical advancements in shaping new gender identities. [BOOKS.GOOGLE.COM](https://books.google.com/books/about/Changing_Sex.html?id=7jYcktA6RhEC&utm_source=chatgpt.com) ![Changing Sex (ebook), Bernice L. Hausman | 9780822396277 | Boeken | bol](https://tse4.mm.bing.net/th?id=OIP.AEg_qEKH_r5joYZvdTf8mwHaJ3&w=200&h=266&c=7)
**Das Geschlecht in mir: Neurowissenschaftliche, lebensweltliche und theologische Beiträge zu Transsexualität**
Edited by Gerhard Schreiber, this publication presents a dialogue between neuroscience, biology, theology, and church perspectives, documenting current research findings and engaging in discussions about ethical, political, and legal engagements with transsexuality. [DEGRUYTER.COM](https://www.degruyter.com/document/doi/10.1515/9783110614626/html?utm_source=chatgpt.com) ![Das Geschlecht in mir](https://tse2.mm.bing.net/th?id=OIP.qyf1bdWF-VQYw7VgjNAJvwHaK_&w=200&h=297&c=7)
**Transsexualität in Theologie und Neurowissenschaften: Ergebnisse, Kontroversen, Perspektiven**
Also edited by Gerhard Schreiber, this book delves into the discoveries, controversies, and perspectives at the intersection of theology and neuroscience concerning transsexuality. [DEGRUYTER.COM](https://www.degruyter.com/document/doi/10.1515/9783110434392/pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com) ![Transsexualität in Theologie und Neurowissenschaften](https://tse4.mm.bing.net/th?id=OIP.Q3RFtialoO5f0o7N9gvVcQHaLA&w=200&h=297&c=7)
**Semiotics: The Basics**
Written by Daniel Chandler, this introductory text demystifies the complex field of semiotics, covering key questions about signs, codes, and the tools semiotics offers for analyzing texts and cultural practices. [TAYLORFRANCIS.COM](https://www.taylorfrancis.com/books/mono/10.4324/9781315311050/semiotics-basics-daniel-chandler?utm_source=chatgpt.com) ![Semiotics: The Basics by Daniel Chandler — Reviews, Discussion, Bookclubs, Lists](https://tse1.mm.bing.net/th?id=OIP.jTSgaKZlmsvyxh69dgZaKgAAAA&w=200&h=306&c=7)
**International Handbook of Semiotics**
Edited by Peter Pericles Trifonas, this comprehensive handbook provides an extensive overview of current work in semiotics across various disciplines, including literature, visual arts, cultural studies, and media. [LINK.SPRINGER.COM](https://link.springer.com/book/10.1007/978-94-017-9404-6?utm_source=chatgpt.com) ![International Handbook of Semiotics | SpringerLink](https://tse2.mm.bing.net/th?id=OIP._FktuCafpowu1TZ8R627NQAAAA&w=184&h=376&c=7)

These selections offer a blend of focused studies on transsexuality and broader explorations of semiotics, providing valuable insights into how meaning and identity are constructed and interpreted.

# table with practical matter for trans people:

Civil name, Surgeries, motherhood, etc

Here's a table outlining practical matters for trans people, covering key areas such as civil name changes, surgeries, and parenthood.

| Category                            | Description                                                                                                            |
| ----------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Civil Name Change                   | Process for legally changing one's name and gender marker on official documents. Varies by country.                    |
| Identification Documents            | Updating passport, ID card, driver’s license, and birth certificate to reflect the affirmed gender.                    |
| Health Insurance Coverage           | Availability of insurance for gender-affirming treatments, including surgeries, HRT, and therapy.                      |
| Hormone Replacement Therapy (HRT)   | Access to testosterone or estrogen therapy, either through informed consent or psychiatric evaluations.                |
| Surgeries                           | Various procedures such as top surgery, bottom surgery, facial feminization surgery (FFS), or masculinization surgery. |
| Motherhood & Parenthood             | Options for preserving fertility (egg/sperm banking), legal recognition of parental status, and adoption rights.       |
| Workplace Rights                    | Protection against discrimination, name/pronoun use at work, and transition-related leave policies.                    |
| Housing & Safety                    | Access to safe housing, shelters, and protection against discrimination in renting or buying property.                 |
| Legal Protections                   | Anti-discrimination laws, hate crime protections, and rights to use public facilities aligned with gender identity.    |
| Mental Health Support               | Access to therapy, support groups, and psychiatric care specializing in gender identity.                               |
| Religious & Cultural Considerations | Navigating gender transition within religious communities and cultural expectations.                                   |
| Sports & Athletics                  | Participation in gendered sports categories, policies of governing sports bodies, and legal disputes.                  |
| Military Service                    | Eligibility to serve, access to gender-affirming care within military healthcare systems.                              |
| Marriage & Partnerships             | Recognition of gender identity in marriage and civil partnerships, impact on existing marriages.                       |
| Sexual Health & Reproductive Rights | Access to trans-inclusive gynecological/urological care, HIV prevention, and PrEP.                                     |
| Community & Advocacy                | Support networks, activism opportunities, and organizations focused on trans rights.                                   |

Would you like this tailored to specific countries or contexts?

# table with subjects challenging to integrate for trans people

Here’s a table outlining subjects that can be challenging for trans people to integrate into their lives, covering legal, medical, social, and personal aspects.

| Category                      | Challenges                                                                                                                                        |
| ----------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Legal Recognition             | Bureaucratic difficulties in changing legal documents, inconsistencies in policies across countries, and legal barriers to gender marker updates. |
| Healthcare Access             | Limited availability of trans-competent healthcare providers, long waiting lists for HRT and surgeries, and lack of insurance coverage.           |
| Mental Health                 | Increased risk of anxiety, depression, dysphoria, and trauma due to social stigma and lack of affirming care.                                     |
| Family Acceptance             | Rejection from family, difficulty in maintaining family relationships, and issues around parental rights.                                         |
| Romantic Relationships        | Challenges in dating due to prejudice, disclosure anxiety, and lack of understanding from partners.                                               |
| Workplace Inclusion           | Employment discrimination, lack of support for transition at work, and difficulty in being recognized by correct name and pronouns.               |
| Religious & Cultural Identity | Conflict between gender identity and religious beliefs, exclusion from faith communities, and cultural taboos around transition.                  |
| Public Safety                 | Increased risk of harassment, violence, and discrimination in public spaces, including bathrooms and transportation.                              |
| Sports Participation          | Barriers to competing in gendered sports categories, exclusion from professional and amateur sports leagues.                                      |
| Reproductive Rights           | Lack of fertility preservation options, barriers to adoption, and misinformation about reproductive health for trans individuals.                 |
| Aging & Elder Care            | Limited access to trans-friendly elder care facilities, higher risk of social isolation in old age.                                               |
| Housing & Homelessness        | Difficulty finding safe and inclusive housing, higher rates of homelessness among trans youth and adults.                                         |
| Sexuality & Identity          | Navigating personal sexual orientation post-transition, misconceptions about trans people's sexualities.                                          |
| Media Representation          | Lack of accurate and respectful trans representation, negative stereotypes in films and journalism.                                               |
| Military Service              | Restrictions on trans people serving in the military, lack of medical support within armed forces.                                                |
| Financial Stability           | Increased financial burden due to medical costs, job discrimination, and difficulty accessing economic opportunities.                             |

Would you like this refined for a specific region or demographic?

# Classification of these subjects in terms of Lacan's RSI

Here’s a classification of the challenges trans people face according to Lacan’s **Real (R), Symbolic (S), and Imaginary (I)** registers:

| Category                      | Challenges                                                               | RSI Classification                                                                                       |
| ----------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Legal Recognition             | Name/gender marker changes, inconsistent policies, bureaucratic hurdles. | Symbolic (S) – Laws, official documentation, and the structure of language shape identity.               |
| Healthcare Access             | Limited trans-competent providers, HRT/surgery access, insurance gaps.   | Real (R) – The body, medical intervention, and its constraints; Symbolic (S) – Institutional frameworks. |
| Mental Health                 | Dysphoria, anxiety, depression, trauma from social stigma.               | Imaginary (I) – Self-image, body perception; Real (R) – The persistence of suffering.                    |
| Family Acceptance             | Rejection, maintaining relationships, parental rights.                   | Symbolic (S) – Family structures and expectations; Imaginary (I) – Identity in the eyes of others.       |
| Romantic Relationships        | Dating struggles, disclosure anxiety, partner misunderstandings.         | Imaginary (I) – Desire, fantasy of love and recognition; Real (R) – The unpredictability of attraction.  |
| Workplace Inclusion           | Discrimination, lack of transition support, misgendering.                | Symbolic (S) – Institutional norms, power dynamics.                                                      |
| Religious & Cultural Identity | Faith-based exclusion, cultural taboos.                                  | Symbolic (S) – Religious discourse; Real (R) – The impossibility of full reconciliation.                 |
| Public Safety                 | Harassment, violence, discrimination in public spaces.                   | Real (R) – The threat of physical violence; Symbolic (S) – Societal laws and norms.                      |
| Sports Participation          | Gendered categories, exclusion from leagues.                             | Symbolic (S) – Institutional rules; Real (R) – The material body’s capacities.                           |
| Reproductive Rights           | Fertility preservation, adoption barriers.                               | Real (R) – Biological constraints; Symbolic (S) – Legal frameworks.                                      |
| Aging & Elder Care            | Lack of inclusive care, social isolation.                                | Symbolic (S) – Institutional neglect; Imaginary (I) – Fear of being forgotten.                           |
| Housing & Homelessness        | Difficulty finding safe housing, high trans homelessness rates.          | Real (R) – Material survival needs; Symbolic (S) – Social structures enabling exclusion.                 |
| Sexuality & Identity          | Navigating orientation post-transition, societal misconceptions.         | Imaginary (I) – Self-perception, attraction; Real (R) – Sexual desire as beyond identity.                |
| Media Representation          | Stereotypes, lack of respectful narratives.                              | Imaginary (I) – Cultural reflections of trans identities.                                                |
| Military Service              | Bans on trans service, lack of medical support.                          | Symbolic (S) – State control, regulations.                                                               |
| Financial Stability           | Economic struggles, job discrimination.                                  | Real (R) – Material survival; Symbolic (S) – Capitalist structures.                                      |

Lacan's RSI model helps highlight how trans experiences oscillate between the **Symbolic** (laws, discourse, social recognition), the **Imaginary** (self-image, fantasy, misrecognition), and the **Real** (bodily experiences, trauma, material conditions).
Would you like any particular aspect to be explored in more depth?

# Art as a solution for the questions above, limits of art and other possible solutions, helpers

**Art as a Solution for Trans Challenges & Its Limits** Art has historically served as a means of **expression, resistance, healing, and reimagining identity** . For trans people facing **legal, social, and existential challenges** , artistic practices offer multiple avenues for integration, self-definition, and political action. However, art has its **limits** , and other structural solutions and allies are necessary to address deeper systemic issues.

---

**1. Art as a Solution in Lacan's RSI Framework**

| Challenge                     | How Art Helps                                                                                           | RSI Classification                                                                        |
| ----------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Legal Recognition             | Creating alternative records (e.g., personal archives, performance art challenging identity documents). | Imaginary (I) – Art as a new self-representation beyond state recognition.                |
| Healthcare Access             | Trans body art, visual storytelling, poetic narratives about transition.                                | Imaginary (I) – Art reshapes body perception; Symbolic (S) – Reframing medical discourse. |
| Mental Health                 | Art therapy, autobiographical works, drag, dance, film.                                                 | Imaginary (I) – Reworking trauma through symbolic expression.                             |
| Family Acceptance             | Theater, poetry, and film offering alternative narratives of trans parenthood, chosen family.           | Symbolic (S) – Creating new cultural scripts for family structures.                       |
| Romantic Relationships        | Music, literature, cinema portraying trans love stories, normalizing trans desire.                      | Imaginary (I) – New fantasies and narratives for love.                                    |
| Workplace Inclusion           | Fashion, makeup, performance challenging gender norms in professional spaces.                           | Symbolic (S) – Art shifts what is seen as "professional."                                 |
| Religious & Cultural Identity | Iconography, ritual performance, reclaiming religious imagery.                                          | Real (R) – Art as an access point to the sacred beyond dogma.                             |
| Public Safety                 | Street art, protests through artistic intervention (e.g., Pussy Riot, Guerrilla Girls).                 | Real (R) – Confronting violence; Symbolic (S) – Shifting public discourse.                |
| Sports Participation          | Digital art, performance challenging binary competition norms.                                          | Imaginary (I) – Redefining what an athlete "should" look like.                            |
| Reproductive Rights           | Experimental cinema, photography exploring trans pregnancy and parenthood.                              | Symbolic (S) – Offering cultural visibility to new family structures.                     |
| Aging & Elder Care            | Memoirs, documentaries preserving trans history, intergenerational art projects.                        | Symbolic (S) – Creating historical continuity.                                            |
| Housing & Homelessness        | Installations, public art raising awareness about trans homelessness.                                   | Real (R) – Confronting material conditions through exposure.                              |
| Sexuality & Identity          | Erotic photography, queer cinema, literature exploring fluid desire.                                    | Imaginary (I) – New representations of trans sexuality.                                   |
| Media Representation          | Independent trans media collectives, zines, podcasts.                                                   | Symbolic (S) – Shifting mainstream narratives.                                            |
| Military Service              | Films, graphic novels documenting trans soldiers' stories.                                              | Symbolic (S) – Rewriting military history.                                                |
| Financial Stability           | NFTs, digital art, alternative economic models for trans artists.                                       | Real (R) – Economic survival through creative work.                                       |

---

**2. Limits of Art as a Solution** While art provides **representation, empowerment, and healing** , it has **structural limitations** :

1. **Material Constraints** – Art cannot replace **legal protections, housing, healthcare, or financial stability** .

2. **Limited Reach** – Not all audiences are receptive to trans narratives in art.

3. **Commodification** – Trans stories can be exploited for profit without real social change.

4. **Censorship & Exclusion** – Trans artists face discrimination in funding, distribution, and institutional acceptance.

5. **The Real as Unrepresentable** – Some traumas resist artistic representation, leaving gaps in expression.

---

**3. Other Possible Solutions & Helpers**

| Solution Type            | Examples                                                          | How It Helps                              |
| ------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------- |
| Legal & Policy Changes   | ID & gender marker reform, workplace protections.                 | Addresses Symbolic (S) barriers.          |
| Community & Mutual Aid   | Trans-led organizations, safe housing programs.                   | Provides Real (R) solutions for survival. |
| Mental Health Services   | Free therapy, trans-competent care.                               | Works on Imaginary (I) integration.       |
| Tech & Digital Platforms | Crowdfunding, NFT markets, decentralized employment.              | Alternative economies for trans people.   |
| Intersectional Activism  | Collaboration with feminist, queer, and racial justice movements. | Expands structural support.               |

---

**4. The Intersection of Art & Structural Solutions** For trans people, **art alone is not enough** , but it plays a key role in **challenging norms, creating alternative realities, and influencing policy** . The most effective approach is a **hybrid one** , where **art fuels activism, shapes discourse, and pushes legal change** .
Would you like me to expand on any particular form of art or specific solutions?
